<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Victoria_Nyanza.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2988" data-file-width="5312" decoding="async" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Victoria_Nyanza.jpg/310px-Victoria_Nyanza.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Victoria_Nyanza.jpg/465px-Victoria_Nyanza.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Victoria_Nyanza.jpg/620px-Victoria_Nyanza.jpg 2x" width="310"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Victoria_Nyanza.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Victoria Nyanza. The black line indicates Stanley's route.</div></div></div>
<p><b>Lake Victoria</b>  is one of the <a href="/wiki/African_Great_Lakes" title="African Great Lakes">African Great Lakes</a>. With a surface area of approximately 59,947 km<sup>2</sup> (23,146 sq mi),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto3_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto3-7">[7]</a></sup> Lake Victoria is Africa's largest lake by area, the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Tropics" title="Tropics">tropical</a> lake,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> and the world's second-largest <a href="/wiki/Fresh_water" title="Fresh water">fresh water</a> lake by surface area after <a href="/wiki/Lake_Superior" title="Lake Superior">Lake Superior</a> in North America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> In terms of volume, Lake Victoria is the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_lakes_by_volume" title="List of lakes by volume">ninth-largest continental lake</a>, containing about 2,424 km<sup>3</sup> (1.965<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">×</span>10<sup>9</sup> acre⋅ft) of water.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto3_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto3-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto4_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto4-10">[10]</a></sup> Lake Victoria occupies a shallow <a href="/wiki/Depression_(geology)" title="Depression (geology)">depression</a> in Africa. The lake has an average depth of 40 m (130 ft) and a maximum depth of 80–84 m (262–276 ft)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto3_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-auto3-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto4_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto4-10">[10]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNEP99_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNEP99-11">[11]</a></sup> Its <a href="/wiki/Drainage_basin" title="Drainage basin">catchment area</a> covers 169,858 km<sup>2</sup> (65,583 sq mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup>  The lake has a shoreline of 7,142 km (4,438 mi) when digitized at the 1:25,000 level,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> with islands constituting 3.7% of this length.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hickling61_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hickling61-14">[14]</a></sup>
</p><p>The lake's area is divided among three countries: <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a> occupies 6% (4,100 km<sup>2</sup> (1,600 sq mi)), <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a> 45% (31,000 km<sup>2</sup> (12,000 sq mi)), and <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a> 49% (33,700 km<sup>2</sup> (13,000 sq mi)).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup>
</p><p>Though having multiple local language names (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dholuo_language" title="Dholuo language">Dholuo</a>: <i lang="luo">Nam Lolwe</i>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luganda_language" title="Luganda language">Luganda</a>: <i lang="lg">'Nnalubaale</i>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kinyarwanda_language" title="Kinyarwanda language">Kinyarwanda</a>: <i lang="rw">Nyanza</i>; also <i>Ukerewe</i>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WDL1_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-WDL1-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> the lake was renamed after <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a> by the explorer <a href="/wiki/John_Hanning_Speke" title="John Hanning Speke">John Hanning Speke</a>, the first <a href="/wiki/British_people" title="British people">Briton</a> to document it in 1858, while on an expedition with <a href="/wiki/Richard_Francis_Burton" title="Richard Francis Burton">Richard Francis Burton</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> 
The lake is home to many species of fish which live nowhere else, especially <a href="/wiki/Cichlid" title="Cichlid">cichlids</a>. <a href="/wiki/Invasive_species" title="Invasive species">Invasive</a> fish, such as the <a href="/wiki/Nile_perch" title="Nile perch">Nile perch</a>, have driven many <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemic</a> species to <a href="/wiki/Extinction" title="Extinction">extinction</a>.
</p>
<div aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading" class="toc" id="toc" role="navigation"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_Victoria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Topography_of_Lake_Victoria.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="889" data-file-width="1360" decoding="async" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Topography_of_Lake_Victoria.png/220px-Topography_of_Lake_Victoria.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Topography_of_Lake_Victoria.png/330px-Topography_of_Lake_Victoria.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Topography_of_Lake_Victoria.png/440px-Topography_of_Lake_Victoria.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Topography_of_Lake_Victoria.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Topographical map of Lake Victoria</div></div></div>
<p>Geologically, Lake Victoria is relatively young at about 400,000 years old. It formed when westward-flowing rivers were dammed by an upthrown crustal block.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reader_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reader-20">[20]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Miocene" title="Miocene">Miocene</a> era, what is now the catchment area of the lake was on the western side of an uplifted area that functioned as a continental divide, with streams on the western side flowing into the <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo River</a> basin and streams on the eastern side flowing to the Indian Ocean. As the <a href="/wiki/East_African_Rift" title="East African Rift">East African Rift</a> System formed, the eastern wall of the <a href="/wiki/Albertine_Rift" title="Albertine Rift">Albertine Rift</a> (or Western Rift) rose, gradually reversing the drainage towards what is now Lake Victoria. The opening of the main East African Rift and the Albertine Rift downwarped the area between them as the rift walls rose, creating the current Lake Victoria basin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> During its geological history, Lake Victoria went through changes ranging from its present shallow depression, through to what may have been a series of much smaller lakes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hickling61_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hickling61-14">[14]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Core_sample" title="Core sample">Geological cores</a> taken from its bottom show Lake Victoria has dried up completely at least three times since it formed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reader_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-Reader-20">[20]</a></sup> These drying cycles are probably related to <a href="/wiki/Quaternary_glaciation" title="Quaternary glaciation">past ice ages</a>, which were times when <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">precipitation</a> declined globally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reader_20-2"><a href="#cite_note-Reader-20">[20]</a></sup> Lake Victoria last dried out about 17,300 years ago, and it refilled 14,700 years ago<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Verheyen2003_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Verheyen2003-22">[22]</a></sup> as the <a href="/wiki/African_humid_period" title="African humid period">African humid period</a> began.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Hydrology_and_limnology">Hydrology and limnology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lake_Victoria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Hydrology and limnology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Lake Victoria receives 80 percent of its water from direct rainfall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hickling61_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-Hickling61-14">[14]</a></sup> Average evaporation on the lake is between 2.0 and 2.2 metres (6.6 and 7.2 ft) per year, almost double the precipitation of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Riparian" title="Riparian">riparian</a> areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Lake Victoria receives its water additionally from rivers, and thousands of small <a href="/wiki/Stream" title="Stream">streams</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Kagera_River" title="Kagera River">Kagera River</a> is the largest river flowing into this lake, with its <a href="/wiki/River_delta" title="River delta">mouth</a> on the lake's western shore. Lake Victoria is drained solely by the <a href="/wiki/Nile" title="Nile">Nile River</a> near Jinja, Uganda, on the lake's northern shore.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fishery_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fishery-25">[25]</a></sup> In the Kenya sector, the main influent rivers are the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sio_River&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Sio River (page does not exist)">Sio</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nzoia" title="Nzoia">Nzoia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yala_River" title="Yala River">Yala</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Nyando_River&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Nyando River (page does not exist)">Nyando</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sondu_Miriu&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Sondu Miriu (page does not exist)">Sondu Miriu</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mogusi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mogusi (page does not exist)">Mogusi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Migori" title="Migori">Migori</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rift_en.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="490" decoding="async" height="269" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Rift_en.svg/220px-Rift_en.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Rift_en.svg/330px-Rift_en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Rift_en.svg/440px-Rift_en.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rift_en.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lake Victoria and the <a href="/wiki/Great_Rift_Valley" title="Great Rift Valley">Great Rift Valley</a></div></div></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1097763485">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output
